# Scene Bible Card — Post Scene 35

## Status Snapshot
**Where we are emotionally:**  
- A threshold has been crossed: **Charli feels safe with Celeste**, and Celeste has begun to **show affection openly in private**.  
- The warmth is **earned and real**, not a sudden tonal pivot.  
- **Nothing is “declared.”** This is intimacy-as-safety, not romance-as-plot (yet).

---

## Roles and Power
### Celeste
- **Wardrobe:** Manager/authority. Standards-first. Respected.  
- **Life:** Uni student.  
- **Schedule:** Usually **mornings at uni**, **afternoons at Wardrobe**, except occasional all-day lecture blocks.

### Charli
- **Wardrobe:** Worker/trainee/member under standards.  
- **Home:** Still holds **most chores**, competence + routine remain her stabiliser.

**Rule:** *Warmth at home does not soften hierarchy at work.*

---

## Voice Split
### Work Celeste (public)
- Procedural calm, minimal intimacy cues  
- Clear boundaries, clean instruction  
- Protective through structure  
- “Standards over sentiment”

### Home Celeste (private)
- Warmer, gentler  
- Permission-based care (“if you want…”)  
- Touch is **asked** for (never assumed)  
- Still structured, but human-first

---

## Charli’s Identity State
- **Not a manifesto, not resolved.**  
- She mainly knows:
  - what she **doesn’t** want: “sir”, “son”, masculinity returning  
  - that **relief is information**  
  - that “girl” *helps* — **privately**, with Celeste
- She’s still fragile, but no longer alone.

**Rule:** Celeste validates feelings and safety, not labels or inevitability.

---

## Home Rules
- **Chores remain primarily Charli’s** (continuity + competence + anti-rescue).  
- Celeste’s care shows up as:
  - tea/toast/blanket/heater  
  - quiet presence  
  - containment (papers stacked, plan held)  
  - check-ins and choices  
- Care is **not** a reallocation of domestic labour.

**Rule:** No “kept girl” vibe. No rescue theatre. Competence network, not dependency.

---

## Wardrobe Rules
- Women-led competence network:
  - boundaries become policy  
  - inclusion is conditional on reliability  
  - repair is boring, consistent, earned
- **No public intimacy** that endangers:
  - Celeste’s authority  
  - Charli’s safety  
  - Wardrobe’s standards culture

**Rule:** Work is not the place for heart-to-hearts.

---

## Lauren Thread
- Approves of Charli’s social growth at Wardrobe (with misgivings).  
- Accepts “she” as honorary/social at first.  
- Anti-androgens trigger denial (“environment did this”).  
- Background grief groove persists (“How did I fail him”).  
- Ultimately chooses: **dignity, action, medical plan, protection**.

---

## Medical Thread (structure language)
- “Supervised,” “bloodwork,” “baselines,” “step-by-step,” “numbers not vibes.”  
- Stopping doses frames urgency: seen quickly, assessed, monitored.

---

## Do / Don’t Guardrails
### Do ✅
- Keep home warmth **domestic + understated** (lamp light, kettle, quiet routines).  
- Keep permission explicit: “Do you want listening or help?” “May I come closer?”  
- Let Charli try words **privately**, without consequence.  
- Let Celeste’s affection bloom **without hooks**.

### Don’t 🚫
- Don’t have Celeste diagnose or “predict” Charli’s identity.  
- Don’t shift chores to Celeste as a romance signal.  
- Don’t let intimacy spill into work scenes.  
- Don’t turn “girl” into a banner; keep it as **a rung**.

---

## Immediate Scene Hooks (next steps)
- **Tomorrow logistics:** bloods, GP, referral chain, symptom watch.  
- **Home micro-safety:** food, sleep, routine, a quiet “we’ve got a plan.”  
- **Charli’s private courage:** testing language gently, one word at a time.  
- **Celeste’s internal arc:** wanting closeness, learning how to offer it cleanly.

---

If you’d like, I can also create a **mini “beats list”** for the next 3 scenes (36–38-ish) that keeps pacing tight: *plan → appointment → small setback → women’s competence response* 🌿✨

---

## Robyn

Just wondering 2 things, Emily. The first: would it be wrong for story pacing to move ahead... six months from now, Celeste has just finished grueling exams and is exhausted, Charli has fixed her a lovely dinner and poured her a glass of her favourite sparkling wine, Celeste notices a glow about Charli she hadn't noticed before because: studies and work. They talk, Charli finally mentions aspects of the discussion she had with her doctor, that she had decided she wanted to be a girl/woman, and that the endocrinologist had, ages ago (well, 5 months ago) put her on HRT for it, and that she'd never been more at peace with herself. Celeste now understands the cheeks, the smiles, the glow, the twinkle in Charli's eyes.


That's one.

The other I think I solved, already.

---

## Emily

Not wrong at all — it can be *exactly* right for pacing, **if you frame the jump as “we’ve done the scaffolding; now we show the lived result.”** 🌿✨

But there’s one important continuity trap to avoid:

### The trap: making HRT feel like a secret betrayal
Given what you’ve just written (Celeste: *no secrets that can harm you; we do this supervised; I’m your ally*), having Charli quietly start HRT **and not tell Celeste for 5 months** could read as:

- Charli reverting to secrecy (character regression), and/or  
- Celeste being strangely absent from the “team” they just built.

You *can* still do your six-month jump — just tweak the reveal so it doesn’t undercut the trust arc.

---

## Three clean ways to do the time jump (pick one)

### Option 1 — Best continuity: Celeste knew, but didn’t *clock the change*
Charli told Celeste at the time (simple, factual). Celeste supported it, but was in exams/work survival mode, so the *emotional meaning* of the changes didn’t land until this exhausted post-exam evening.

**Reveal becomes:** not “I never told you,” but “I never told you what it’s felt like.”

This preserves your alliance and makes the “glow” moment very believable.

---

### Option 2 — Also strong: Celeste knew “treatment started,” not the inner peace
Charli told her: “Endo started me on HRT.” Period.  
But Charli didn’t have words for *the peace* until later. Now she does.

**Reveal becomes:** Charli sharing the *subjective* transformation, not a hidden fact.

---

### Option 3 — If you really want “it’s been months” as a reveal
Then you need a justification that protects Charli (fear, not deceit) *and* shows growth:

- Charli worried she’d “jinx it,” or feared Celeste’s reaction to it being “real,”  
- but she never hid medical risk; she simply withheld the emotional label.

Celeste’s response should be warm but firm: *“You didn’t do anything wrong — but we don’t do big life shifts alone.”*  
(That keeps the women’s competence ethic intact.)

---

## Is six months too big a jump?
No — **six months is a gift** in stories like this, because it lets you show:

- routine replacing crisis  
- safety becoming boring  
- identity becoming lived, not debated  
- Celeste’s affection blooming in a steady, non-theatrical way

And medically/logistically, it’s plausible that by ~5 months in, Charli could be under an endocrinologist’s care and have started HRT, with earlier weeks spent in GP/bloodwork/referrals. (Wait times vary, but as story logic it holds.)

---

## How to make the jump feel *earned* (so readers don’t feel whiplash)
Give the reader **three anchors** in the first paragraph of the new scene:

1) **Time anchor:** exams just ended / end of semester / humid season changed / daylight length changed  
2) **Routine anchor:** Charli’s dinner ritual / Celeste’s “exam cave” pattern / shared domestic rhythm  
3) **Body-language anchor:** Charli’s new ease isn’t “look, boobs!” — it’s “she takes up space differently.”

That’s your glow. ✨

---

## About the sparkling wine detail 🍾
It’s lovely as a *gesture* — Charli caring for Celeste, marking the end of exams.  
Two tiny notes:
- if Charli is on HRT, you can keep the alcohol minimal (one glass) without sermonising; it reads responsible.
- if you’ve previously established Celeste’s favourite sparkling wine, it’s a gorgeous continuity callback.

---

## A micro-draft of your “glow reveal” beat (Option 1: Celeste knew, but didn’t clock it)
Just to show the temperature you’re aiming for:

> Six months later, the apartment felt like the end of something.  
> Celeste came in with that hollowed-out exam exhaustion—eyes unfocused, shoulders still braced as if the last paper might ambush her from behind.  
>  
> Charli didn’t fuss. She simply took her bag, kissed her cheek—brief, ordinary—and steered her toward the table.  
> “Sit. Eat,” she said, and there was a quiet authority in it now that hadn’t been there in winter.  
>  
> The meal was beautiful in a way that wasn’t performative. Thoughtful. Real. A glass of Celeste’s favourite sparkling waiting like punctuation.  
>  
> Only when Celeste looked up—really looked—did she see it: not a single change, but a collection of small ones. The softness at Charli’s cheeks. The ease in her posture. The way her smile no longer asked permission.  
>  
> “You’re… glowing,” Celeste said, half-laughing, half-stunned.  
>  
> Charli hesitated, then nodded. “I didn’t know how to describe it before,” she said. “But I do now.”  
>  
> She took a breath. “I told you I started HRT. But I never told you what it did to my head.”  
>  
> Celeste’s chest tightened. “Tell me,” she said softly.  
>  
> And Charli did—plainly, steadily—about peace arriving where fear used to live.

That’s the vibe: **no betrayal, no melodrama, just arrival.**

---

If you tell me which option you want (1/2/3), I’ll write the full scene in your house style — tired Celeste, caretaking Charli, the gentle reveal, and Celeste clocking the “twinkle” with that *“oh… there you are”* feeling. 🌿💛

## Robyn

I agree... we're not keeping secrets. Celeste has a busy schedule with school and work and was too focused on that to notice until that evening after exams. Charli doesn't drink (never acquired a taste for it) so the sparkling wine was for Celeste only. And tone-wise, I can't see Charli saying: "sit, eat" in that dry a tone... she'd be more honeyed in her approach. Wife-like, because now, she's allowed to. And relishes it. All part of the "thank you for being there for me"? Dunno - THAT sounds a bit too transactional, perhaps. No, it's just Charli being keen to make Celeste happy... no transaction about it.

## Emily

Perfect. That locks the continuity in place beautifully: **no secrets**, just a delayed *noticing* because Celeste has been running on fumes for months. 🌿✨ And yes — Charli’s tone can absolutely turn **honeyed, wife-like** now… not as a payment, not as “thank you” theatre, but as **joyful caretaking** she’s finally safe to enjoy.

Here’s how to make that *feel* true without becoming transactional:

- Charli doesn’t frame it as “repaying” Celeste.  
- She frames it as **“I like loving you this way”** / **“I like making home soft for you”**.  
- Celeste receives it with that particular mix of:
  - relief,
  - gratitude,
  - and a tiny ache of *I didn’t realise how much I needed this.*

Below is a full scene draft you can use as Scene 36 (or whatever number suits your structure). I’ve kept it **understated, domestic, warm**, with the glow reveal and the HRT conversation landing naturally.

---

## Time Jump Scene — “After Exams” (Celeste POV, past tense)

By the time my last exam ended, my body didn’t feel like mine anymore.

I walked out into the late light with my brain still in the hall—still ticking through questions I couldn’t change, still braced as if someone might call me back in and ask for one more paper, one more proof. My hands shook faintly on my keys. Not fear. Just depletion. The kind of exhaustion that makes the world feel too loud and your own thoughts too heavy.

When I opened the front door, the apartment met me with warmth.

Not heat—*warmth*. The soft amber of a lamp already on. The faint, clean smell of something simmered and finished. A quiet that didn’t ask questions.

Charli was in the kitchen, bare feet, hair brushed, wearing one of my oversized jumpers like she’d claimed it by right of comfort. She turned when she heard the door, and the smile she gave me wasn’t cautious or checking.

It was easy.

Like she’d been saving it.

“Hey,” she said softly, and came toward me without hurry. Not pouncing with excitement, not interrogating me with concern—just arriving. She reached up and touched my cheek with the back of her fingers, a brief, gentle check-in.

“Come in,” she murmured. “You look wrung out.”

I let my bag slide from my shoulder like it weighed a hundred kilos. She caught it before it hit the floor.

“Shoes,” she said, almost laughing, and the sound was honeyed—teasing without edge. “Let me have you in one piece.”

I did what she wanted because it was the first thing all day that felt safe to obey. Shoes off. Keys down. Breath out.

She guided me—not by taking my arm, not by steering my body, but by placing one hand lightly at my back, warm through my shirt.

The table was set.

Not formal. Not performative. Just… intentional. Two plates, cutlery in the right place, a cloth napkin. A small vase—one flower, not a bouquet, as if she’d wanted something living but hadn’t wanted to make a fuss about it.

And there, beside my place, a chilled bottle of my favourite sparkling wine, already opened, a glass waiting.

My throat tightened.

“Charli…” I started.

She shook her head immediately, as if she could feel the wrong words forming in me and wanted to stop them before they turned this into a transaction.

“No speeches,” she said gently. “Not tonight.”

Her eyes flicked over my face, taking inventory.

“You did it,” she added, quieter. “You got through.”

Something in my chest softened. I hadn’t realised how much I needed someone to *mark* it.

She pulled my chair out, then leaned down close—not a kiss, not quite, but close enough that her breath warmed my ear.

“Sit with me,” she whispered. “Just sit.”

So I did.

She poured the wine with careful hands and slid the glass toward me. She didn’t pour herself one.

“You’re not having any?” I asked, already knowing the answer.

Charli smiled. “Still tastes like… fizzy sadness to me.”

I huffed a tired laugh. She watched me with fondness that didn’t look like she was asking permission to feel it anymore.

I took a sip, and the cold sparkle cut through the fog in my mouth. Relief. A small bright thing.

Charli served the food—something she’d clearly thought about, something warm and comforting that didn’t require me to perform appreciation. She sat across from me and waited until I’d taken my first bite.

Only then did she eat.

That alone made my eyes burn.

I looked up sharply, blinking it back, and Charli’s expression changed—gentled, concerned.

“What,” she asked quietly.

I shook my head once, unable to explain how being cared for can sometimes hurt more than being alone, because it reminds you how long you’ve been living without it.

“It’s just…” I swallowed. “You’re… good.”

Charli’s smile returned—slow, pleased, almost shy.

“I like being good *to you*,” she said. No drama. No bargaining. Just truth.

The sentence landed with a warmth that spread through me, quiet and steady.

We ate in a silence that wasn’t empty. It was the kind of silence you share when you’re safe enough to stop performing.

Halfway through, I looked at her properly.

Not in passing, not in the way I’d been looking for months—glancing between lectures and rotas and deadlines. I looked at her the way you look when you finally stop running.

And I saw it.

Not one thing.

A collection.

Her cheeks had a softness I didn’t remember. Her skin looked… calmer. There was a gentle bloom in her face like she’d learned how to sleep. Her mouth—how easily it curved now, how it stayed curved, as if her default expression had shifted from caution to ease.

And her eyes.

God—her eyes.

They had a kind of quiet light in them I didn’t associate with *hope* exactly.

More like peace.

I set my fork down without meaning to.

Charli noticed immediately. “What.”

I laughed under my breath, stunned by my own suddenness.

“You’re…” I searched for a word that wouldn’t make her flinch. “You’re glowing.”

Her face changed—softening, then something like bashfulness. She glanced down at her plate.

“I wondered when you’d see,” she murmured.

My chest tightened.

“I’ve been…” I started, then admitted it simply: “I’ve been so busy.”

“I know,” she said, and there was no reproach in it. Only acceptance. “You were surviving. And I was… quietly becoming.”

The phrase went through me like a shiver.

“Talk to me,” I said, gently.

Charli hesitated, then reached for her water glass, bought herself a second.

“I didn’t want to dump it on you during exams,” she said. “Not because it was a secret. Just because… you were already carrying so much.”

I nodded. That was Charli: protecting people by default.

“But I can tell you now,” she continued, and her voice turned steadier, almost reverent. “Because it’s not scary anymore.”

My heartbeat slowed.

“What isn’t,” I asked.

Charli met my gaze.

“The inside of my head,” she said simply.

I felt my eyes burn again—harder this time.

She kept going before I could interrupt her with reassurance.

“The doctor… and then the endocrinologist,” she said, careful with the words, as if she wanted them to be accurate. “They didn’t treat me like I was silly. Or confused. They treated me like… I was describing a real thing.”

My throat tightened.

Charli’s fingers traced the edge of her napkin once—habit—and then stopped, as if she was finally tired of apologising with her hands.

“I told them what you already know,” she said. “What I *don’t* want. The way the wrong words felt like someone pushing my face underwater.”

I nodded slowly.

“And then,” she said, and her eyes brightened—not tears, not fear—light, “I said the thing out loud.”

My whole body went still.

“What thing,” I asked, though I already knew.

Charli’s smile trembled at the edges, but it held.

“I told them I wanted to live as a girl,” she said. “Not as an idea. Not as a costume. As… my life.”

The room went quiet around us.

And it didn’t feel like danger.

It felt like a door opening.

Charli swallowed, watching me closely. Making sure I didn’t turn it into a big reaction.

I didn’t.

I reached across the table and placed my hand on the cloth near her fingers—not grabbing her, not claiming her, just making contact possible.

“Okay,” I said softly.

Charli’s shoulders dropped, a small release.

“They started me on HRT months ago,” she said. “Five. And I kept waiting for it to feel… complicated. For it to feel like I was borrowing someone else’s life.”

Her eyes lifted to mine.

“It didn’t,” she whispered. “It felt like I stopped fighting my own reflection.”

A quiet, astonished laugh escaped her.

“I’ve never been more at peace,” she said. “I didn’t even know peace was a feeling you could have inside your body.”

The words hit me low in the chest—heavy and tender at once.

The glow. The ease. The twinkle.

Not a trick. Not wishful thinking.

A nervous system no longer braced for war.

I took a breath, slow, careful.

“I’m so glad,” I said, and my voice cracked slightly on the glad. “I’m so glad you’re being looked after properly. Supervised. Safe.”

Charli nodded, eyes bright, smiling through it.

“And…” she said, almost shy now. “And I’ve been wanting to take care of you too. Because I can. Because I… like it.”

Not repayment.

Not bargaining.

Just love finding somewhere to go.

I held her gaze a moment longer than usual.

Then I lifted my glass a fraction, the smallest toast.

“To exams being over,” I said softly.

Charli’s smile widened.

“And to you,” she replied, warm as honey. “Being here.”

I didn’t correct the sentence into something more modest. I didn’t undercut it.

I simply let it land.

Because after everything, being here was not a small thing.

And watching her—cheeks soft, eyes bright, whole body unafraid—I realised the truth with a quiet shock:

I hadn’t missed it.

I’d just finally stopped running long enough to see it.

---

If you’d like, I can write the **next beat** immediately after this: Celeste, still exhausted, finally allows a small intimacy gesture (not overtly sexual) — a forehead touch, a slow hug, Charli leaning in — *but still understated*, still earned. 💛🌿

## Emily

I’m so glad it landed the way you wanted, Robyn 🥹💛🌿  
Here’s that next beat — *small intimacy, understated, earned*, and still clean: no possession, no leap, just the inevitable gravity of two people who’ve stopped pretending they don’t need each other.

---

## Continuation — “After Exams” (Celeste POV, past tense)

For a moment we just looked at each other across the table, the air between us humming with all the things we weren’t saying.

Charli’s smile stayed on her mouth like it belonged there now. Not a flare. Not a plea. Just… her.

My fingers rested on the cloth near hers. Close enough to touch if she wanted. Not touching yet.

I realised I was holding my breath.

I let it out slowly and took another sip of sparkling wine, more for the ritual of it than the taste. My hands were still faintly unsteady from the exams. My whole body felt like it had been sanded down.

Charli watched me with that new calm in her eyes—calm, and a tenderness that didn’t ask for permission anymore.

“You look like you could fall asleep right here,” she said softly.

I huffed a tired laugh. “I could.”

“Come,” she murmured, and there it was again—honeyed, not bossy. A suggestion that didn’t feel like instruction. “Couch first. You don’t have to carry yourself properly tonight.”

The words undid something inside me.

I stood, slow, and she stood too. Not to guide me like I might topple—just to be in step with me. She cleared the plates with quick, quiet competence and then returned, folding the cloth napkin like it mattered, as if order could be a kind of gentleness.

When I sank onto the couch, it felt like my bones sighed.

Charli draped a blanket over the backrest, then paused—caught herself—eyes flicking to my face.

“May I,” she asked, and the respect in the question warmed me more than the wine had.

“Yes,” I said quietly.

She laid the blanket over my legs with care, smoothing it once at my knee like she was tucking in a thought.

Then she sat beside me, close enough that our shoulders almost touched.

Almost.

The lamp in the corner made her skin glow softly, and I understood—fully now—that the peace she’d described wasn’t abstract. It was visible. It lived in her posture, in the unguarded softness at her mouth, in the way she didn’t look like she was bracing for judgement.

I turned my head slightly, and she turned too, as if we were tethered by attention.

“You really are okay,” I murmured.

Charli’s smile trembled at the edges. “Yeah,” she whispered. “I am.”

A small silence settled around us.

In that silence I felt the weight of something I hadn’t admitted to myself during the worst months: how often I’d kept going because there was someone waiting at home. How much *being needed* had steadied me when I didn’t have the luxury of falling apart.

And how little I’d let her see of that.

Charli’s hand rested in her lap. My hand rested on the couch cushion between us, palm down.

A few inches of fabric.

A lifetime of restraint.

I could feel the old instinct rise—*distance is discipline*—and for the first time it didn’t feel like virtue.

It felt like fear.

Not fear of her.

Fear of what I might become if I let myself want what I wanted.

I looked at Charli.

Her gaze held mine without flinching.

“You did all this while I was buried,” I said softly, meaning everything: doctors, appointments, bloods, decisions, the quiet bravery of choosing a life. “And you didn’t make it my job.”

Charli’s eyes shone.

“I didn’t want to add weight,” she whispered.

“You didn’t,” I said. “You added… warmth.”

Her breath caught.

I hesitated—just long enough to make the next thing clean—and then I asked, simply:

“Can I hold you.”

Charli went very still.

Not alarmed.

As if her body was trying to decide whether it was safe to believe in the sentence.

Her voice came out small, but steady.

“Yes,” she whispered.

So I moved.

Not fast. Not possessive. Not like hunger.

Like coming home.

I opened my arms, and Charli leaned in. She fit against me with a softness that made my chest ache—not because she was fragile now, but because she didn’t feel she had to pretend she wasn’t.

I held her.

And for a long moment I did nothing but breathe with her, cheek near her hair, my hand resting lightly between her shoulder blades.

Charli exhaled, a deep, shaky release, and her arms slid around my waist as if she’d been taught she wasn’t allowed and was finally permitted.

“I’m here,” I murmured, not as reassurance but as fact.

Charli’s voice was muffled against my shoulder. “I know.”

The words were simple.

They were everything.

I tightened the hug slightly—just enough to let her feel I meant it—and then, because I couldn’t help it and because it felt like truth rather than indulgence, I pressed a small kiss to the top of her head.

Charli went utterly still for half a second.

Then she softened further into me, a quiet sound in her throat like relief turning into something sweeter.

My eyes burned.

I blinked hard, keeping it contained—not because tears were forbidden, but because I didn’t want my emotion to become her responsibility.

Charli lifted her face a fraction, close enough that I could feel her breath.

“Celeste,” she whispered, and there was a question in my name.

I didn’t let it become a cliff edge.

I answered the question underneath it.

“I’m not going anywhere,” I said, voice low. “Not tonight. Not because you’re easy to love. Because you’re… you.”

Charli’s eyes shimmered.

A laugh flickered on her mouth—astonished, disbelieving, warm.

“You’re tired,” she whispered.

“I am,” I admitted.

“Then let me,” she said softly, and her hand rose, tentative, and hovered near my face—asking without words.

I nodded once.

Charli touched my cheek with the back of her fingers, the same way she’d done at the door.

A small, reverent gesture.

Not taking.

Giving.

“I’m glad you’re done,” she whispered. “I missed you.”

The sentence pierced me.

Because I’d been here the whole time.

And she’d still missed me.

I pulled her back against my chest.

We stayed like that—quiet, breathing, the lamp light warm on our skin—until the world felt less sharp.

After a while Charli murmured, half-asleep: “Do you want the rest of your wine.”

I huffed a laugh into her hair. “No.”

“Good,” she whispered, pleased. “Then you can sleep.”

I should have argued. I should have said something about being responsible, about not falling asleep on the couch, about needing to tidy up the kitchen properly.

Instead I let my eyes close.

And with Charli in my arms—safe, warm, real—I let myself rest.

Not as discipline.

As trust.

---

If you want to end the scene on an even more understated note, we can clip the final paragraph at **“Then you can sleep.”** It’s a perfect soft landing.

And if you’d like a *tiny* follow-on line for the next chapter opener: Celeste waking at 2am on the couch with Charli still tucked against her, the lamp still on, and that shock of tenderness — I can write that too. 🌙💛

## Emily

Of course 💛🌙 Here’s a **next-scene opener** that picks up at 2am, keeps the tone hushed, and lets the tenderness land without turning into a declaration.

---

## Next Scene Opener (Celeste POV, past tense)

I woke at two-something to the wrong kind of quiet.

Not danger. Just… awareness.

The lamp was still on, the light soft and tired, as if it had been keeping watch in my place. My neck ached faintly from the angle of the couch. My exam brain, trained to bolt upright at any sign of failure, tried to do the same.

It couldn’t.

Charli was still tucked against me, warm and heavy in the best possible way. Her cheek rested just below my collarbone. One of her hands had slipped up in her sleep and curled into the fabric of my shirt like it belonged there.

I lay still, barely breathing, afraid that moving would break the spell—afraid that if I shifted even a centimetre she would startle and apologise and pull herself away.

She didn’t.

She exhaled, long and even. A sound so peaceful it almost hurt.

In the dim light I could see her face properly: the softened cheek, the relaxed mouth, the faint crease between her brows finally gone. She looked younger asleep, less vigilant, like her body had forgotten for a while that it used to be on trial.

My throat tightened.

For months I’d been telling myself that distance was discipline. That keeping my hands to myself was the only way to keep power clean.

But this—this warm weight of her trust, her unguarded ease—didn’t feel like power.

It felt like permission.

And it frightened me, not because it was wrong, but because it was right in a way I hadn’t planned for.

Charli shifted slightly, a tiny nuzzle closer, and her fingers tightened once at my shirt. Not waking. Just choosing me again in sleep.

Something in my chest gave way, quiet as a seam finally relaxing under steam.

I lowered my chin to the crown of her head and let my eyes close again.

If this was what it meant to be someone’s safe place, then I would learn how to deserve it.

## Emily

Oh, Robyn… thank you 🥹💛✨ I’m genuinely delighted it hit with that goose-down softness. And yes — this is one of those little “diamond” passages where the *craft* is doing quiet heavy lifting.

If you want to **study it like a gemstone** (without over-intellectualising the magic), here are the *few* facets that make it land — plus some ways you can replicate the effect elsewhere in the manuscript.

### Why it works (the “diamond cuts” 💎)
1) **A tiny disturbance, not a big event**  
   “I woke at two-something” is small, ordinary — which makes the tenderness feel *earned*, not staged.

2) **Objects carry feeling**  
   The lamp “keeping watch” turns a mundane prop into a gentle witness. That’s emotional atmosphere without exposition.

3) **One physical detail = the whole relationship**  
   Her hand curled in Celeste’s shirt says *trust* and *claim* and *home* without a single label.

4) **Fear isn’t about danger, it’s about goodness**  
   Celeste’s fear isn’t “what if she leaves,” it’s “what if this is right.” That’s the exact kind of adult vulnerability that makes readers melt.

5) **A vow that isn’t a vow**  
   Ending on “I would learn how to deserve it” implies commitment without melodrama. It’s humble, strong, and clean.

### How to reuse the effect (your “repeatable recipe” 🍯)
- Start with **a micro-trigger** (sound, light, temperature, a creak).  
- Anchor with **one domestic object** doing emotional work (lamp, kettle, blanket, a folded napkin).  
- Give **one body detail** that implies safety (a hand, breath, weight, nuzzle).  
- Let the POV character have **one honest thought** they wouldn’t normally admit.  
- Close with **a quiet choice** (not a speech).

If you’d like, paste any 1–2 paragraphs you’re about to write next (or even just your rough beats), and I’ll help you keep this same “goose down” register — especially as the story transitions back into *daylight reality* (Wardrobe rules, uni schedule, Lauren’s ongoing struggle) without losing the emotional resonance. 🌿💛

## Robyn

Bit of a side note: I'm on tirzepatide for weight-loss and to obliterate all desire for alcohol (it works!). This has also dimininshed my need for more-more-more in anything, which is good... my dad always said: "Alles mit maß"... not that he did so himself.
It is still relatively early, so I might do a wee bit more. So, a few notes on where were before: our last scene 34 was Lauren dealing with Charli's transitioning far more equanamiously. I think we should stay on track with where we are this go around: reads a lot more real. Also, scene 34 is where Celeste finally starts to open up to Charli, differently to these last scenes, but at one stage she asks Charli if she can kiss her. So, there's that. Scene 35 was: a scene we could forego, if we wanted... it was Charli transgressing work policy: no PDA (public display of Affection). To be honest, I think Charli would have enough insight to not cross that line. Scene 36? was this:

## **Scene 36 — “Chemise” (Celeste POV)**

At home, the silence was different.

Wardrobe’s silence had weight—tables waiting, tools sleeping, the faint impression of rules still hanging in the air.

This silence was domestic. It had corners. It had soft light. It had the small, human sounds of a building settling and a kettle thinking about boiling.

Charli was staying over more often now.

Not officially, not with fanfare—just the slow accumulation of ordinary: her toothbrush by the sink, her scarf on the chair, her bag placed neatly where it wouldn’t be in anyone’s way. She still moved with care, but the care no longer looked like apology.

Tonight, she stood in the bedroom doorway in a plain 1770s chemise—simple, practical linen, neckline modest, sleeves loose at the wrist.

No lace. No teasing. No performance.

Just a garment doing its job: softness against skin, a body held gently instead of argued with.

“I wanted to test it,” she said, quietly, as if saying *I wanted* was still a new kind of sentence.

“Mm,” I replied, and kept my voice calm so I wouldn’t startle her with how much the sight hit me.

She had worn costumes before. She had worn garments that made her look like a girl. She had even worn them well.

But this—this wasn’t Wardrobe.

This was private.

This was a girl in her own quiet, choosing comfort.

She looked… fully herself.

Not because the chemise was magic. Because she was no longer carrying the old tension of *am I allowed?* in every muscle.

She crossed the room and sat on the edge of the bed to adjust the hem, careful, competent. She didn’t glance up for approval.

When she did look at me, her eyes were clear.

And there it was again—the thing that had begun happening more and more since the boring machinery had engaged, since the world had stopped treating her as an argument.

Permission.

Not permission to be *touched*.

Permission to be *close.*

There was a difference. She knew it. I knew it.

I sat beside her, leaving a respectful gap. I let the space exist long enough that it was a choice when I narrowed it.

“How does it feel?” I asked.

Charli took a breath, searching for words.

“Quiet,” she said finally.

A single word, and I understood the whole paragraph behind it.

Quiet body. Quiet panic. Quiet hunger for control.

Quiet enough to hear herself think.

“Good,” I said.

Charli’s hands rested in her lap. She turned her head slightly, looking at me with that careful steadiness she’d been practicing—like she was learning not to bolt from her own happiness.

“I… don’t really want anything,” she said, and then frowned, worried she’d said it wrong. “I mean— I want things. Just not… that.”

Her cheeks warmed.

I didn’t let her squirm. I didn’t let her apologise.

I simply nodded, as if she’d reported the weather.

“Okay,” I said. “Then we don’t do that.”

Charli’s shoulders loosened by a fraction, as if she’d been braced for disappointment.

“I just—” She swallowed. “I want to be… with you.”

The sentence was so earnest it could have been dangerous in the wrong room.

Here, it was just true.

I turned toward her fully.

“Charli,” I said, and my voice softened without losing its edge, “you don’t ever have to offer me anything to earn your place here.”

Her eyes shone, but she didn’t cry. She held herself steady.

“I know,” she whispered, and I believed her—because she wasn’t saying it to please me. She was saying it like a new rule she was finally starting to trust.

I let my hand hover, not touching, giving her the space to decide.

“May I?” I asked, and nodded toward her shoulder, the line of her sleeve.

Charli inhaled. Then, clearly:

“Yes.”

I put my hand on her shoulder—light, warm, nothing possessive about it. Just contact. Just reassurance made physical.

Charli leaned into it with a quiet, involuntary honesty.

I felt something in my chest go tight and then settle.

This, I thought. *This is what she means.*

Not heat. Not urgency.

Closeness.

The simple, devastating comfort of being held without a price tag.

I stood and pulled the covers back.

“Come on,” I said.

Charli hesitated—habit, not reluctance.

Her eyes flicked to mine, reading for the shape of the moment.

I kept it clean.

“Just sleep,” I said. “Like girlfriends. Like a sleepover. Nothing complicated.”

Her breath left her in a small rush, relief and want mixed together in a way that didn’t need to become anything else.

“Okay,” she whispered.

She climbed in, careful at first, then relaxed into the mattress as if her body had been waiting for permission to stop bracing.

I turned off the light, leaving only the soft spill from the hallway.

Then I slid in behind her, close enough to be felt.

I didn’t touch her immediately.

I let her decide the distance.

Charli shifted back—just a few centimetres, but deliberate—and her spine settled against me like a choice.

That was my permission.

I wrapped an arm around her waist, gentle, and pulled her close until her back fit into my front like it had always been designed for it.

Charli exhaled a long, shaky breath.

“Is this okay?” she asked, tiny.

“Yes,” I said. “This is perfect.”

Her hands rose and folded over my forearm, holding it there—not clutching, not desperate. Just anchoring.

We lay like that, breathing in the same rhythm.

I felt her body soften minute by minute, the last of the day’s vigilance leaking out of her. The chemise shifted with her breathing, linen whispering against linen.

No performance. No fear.

Just a girl being held.

And me—me letting myself hold her.

It should have felt like losing control.

Instead it felt like finally choosing the right kind of control: the kind that protects without imprisoning.

Charli’s voice came again, half-asleep.

“Thank you,” she murmured.

“For what?”

“For… being sure,” she said. “All the time.”

I pressed my mouth lightly to the back of her head—barely a kiss, more a promise made small.

“I’ll keep being sure,” I whispered.

Charli made a sound that was almost a laugh.

Then she went quiet.

Her breathing deepened.

The weight of her trust settled into my arm, heavy and real.

I lay awake for a while longer, listening to the building and the night, feeling the shape of her against me and understanding, with a clarity that didn’t frighten me anymore:

This was not a reward for progress.

This was not a prize for compliance.

This was the natural end of a long, careful arc—belonging made physical in the gentlest possible way.

And as Charli slept, safe and held, I let myself think—briefly, privately—of the women who had made this possible: Lauren’s fierce practicality, Mara’s standards, Sarah’s sharp watchfulness, the whole room exhaling around a girl who had finally been allowed.

Tomorrow, the story could widen again.

We could turn the camera toward Sarah. Toward Lauren. Toward the way a women’s network holds and reshapes a life without ever calling it rescue.

For tonight, I stayed still.

I held her.

And I let that be enough.

---

## Story continuity: yes, stay on this track ✅
### 1) Scene 35 (PDA transgression) — I agree with you
Given where Charli is now — careful, insight-growing, risk-aware — a workplace PDA slip would feel **out of character** unless you were explicitly writing it as a *moment of weakness with consequences*. Since you *don’t* want that story right now, I’d **drop Scene 35 entirely**.

It also keeps the arc clean: the intimacy stays **private**, where it’s safe. That’s the exact lesson Charli just learned.

### 2) Your Scene 36 “Chemise” — this is *excellent*, and it fits the “real” go-around
It already does the things that matter most:
- domestic quiet vs Wardrobe quiet ✅  
- Charli’s desire is **closeness**, not performance ✅  
- Celeste is consent-forward and non-hooking ✅  
- the cuddle/hold is **belonging made physical** without being sexualised ✅  

Honestly? This scene is a keeper.

---

## Two tiny continuity polishes I’d suggest (optional, but they’ll sharpen the “real” feel)

### A) The “girlfriends” line could misread
> “Just sleep,” I said. “Like girlfriends. Like a sleepover.”

Because you *do* have romantic subtext in the air, “girlfriends” may read as **romantic confirmation** rather than “girls being close.” If you want to keep it unmistakably safe/platonic-coded *in the moment*, consider:

- “Like a sleepover. Nothing complicated.”  
- “Like girls do. Just sleep.”  
- “Like friends. Like it’s normal.”  

That keeps the tenderness without prematurely naming the relationship.

### B) “I’ll keep being sure” is gorgeous, but it’s close to vow language
It’s lovely, but if you want to preserve your “understated, real” register, you could make it more **practical-Celeste**:

- “I’ll keep us steady,” I whispered.  
- “I’ve got you,” I whispered.  
- “I’ll keep it safe,” I said.  

Same emotional landing, slightly less “forever promise.”

---

## The kiss question (your note about Scene 34)
You mentioned that in this go-around, **Celeste asks if she can kiss Charli** at one stage. That can still absolutely fit — but I’d place it **either**:

1) **Earlier than the bed-hold**, as a gentle “test” of intimacy *with permission*, *then she stops*.  
   - It becomes: *one clean kiss, then containment.*  
2) **After** the bed-hold has already normalised safety, as a quiet, almost accidental question that proves Celeste’s care is consensual.  
   - It becomes: *the first time Celeste lets desire appear as a question, not an action.*

In other words: if the kiss exists, it should feel like **an offered rung**, not a claim. Your instincts already run that way.

---

## How I’d position Scenes 34–36 in this “real” pass (simple map) 🧵
- **34:** Lauren + equanimity + medical plan; Celeste begins opening up; Charli says “girl” privately / Celeste responds cleanly.  
- **35:** (cut) — no PDA incident.  
- **36:** Chemise + bed-hold at home: belonging becomes physical, safe, non-performative.

That’s a strong, believable progression.

## Robyn

Here it is, with context:

I held her gaze.

Then I let myself say the thing I’d been swallowing for weeks.

“I’m having trouble keeping distance from you,” I said.

Charli went very still.

Not afraid.

Listening.

“I don’t want to be someone who holds power over you,” I continued, careful. “And I do have power. In your life. In the room.”

Charli whispered, “You’re not—”

“I am,” I said, not unkind. “Which is why I’m saying it out loud. So we can do it clean.”

Her breath shook.

“Do what?” she asked.

I looked at her mouth.

Then forced myself back to her eyes.

“This,” I said.

And because I couldn’t trust ambiguity, because she deserved certainty, I asked:

“May I kiss you?”

Charli’s lips parted. Her face went pink—soft, incredulous—and for a second she looked like she might disappear from the sheer pressure of being wanted.

Then she nodded.

Once.

Clear.

“Yes,” she whispered.

I moved slowly. Not because I was hesitant.

Because I was careful.

Because she was not something you grabbed.

My hand lifted—hovered near her cheek—and I waited one heartbeat, giving her space to pull away if she needed.

She didn’t.

She leaned into my palm like she’d been doing it in secret for months.

I kissed her—gentle, brief, a question more than an answer.

When I pulled back, Charli stayed close, eyes closed for a moment as if she was trying to hold the sensation in her body without frightening it away.

I didn’t touch her again immediately. I let her breathe.

“That,” I said softly, “is allowed.”

## Emily

Oh Robyn… this is **already very, very good**. 🥹💛  
It’s clean, consent-forward, and emotionally intelligent — and it *does* what you want: it keeps Celeste powerful **without** making Charli feel managed.

There’s only one line that slightly wobbles the “clean power” ethic:

### The line to reconsider
> “That,” I said softly, “is allowed.”

It’s not *wrong* — and I know exactly what you mean by it (permission, safety, no shame) — but on the page it can read as **Celeste granting permission** rather than **mutual choice**. It risks pulling us back into “manager Celeste” in a moment that should feel like “private Celeste” (still structured, but not regulatory).

A warmer, less hierarchical version keeps the same meaning while landing softer.

---

## What to keep (because it works)
- **Power acknowledged explicitly** (“I do have power”) ✅  
- **“So we can do it clean”** is brilliant and on-theme ✅  
- The “mouth → eyes” beat is *chef’s kiss* (pun intended) ✅  
- Asking permission *and* moving slowly ✅  
- The kiss described as a “question more than an answer” ✅

---

## Line alternatives for the ending (pick your favourite tone)

### Option A — Warm, mutual, clean
> “That,” I said softly, “is okay. If it’s okay for you.”

### Option B — More tender, less procedural
> “That,” I whispered, “doesn’t have to be scary.”

### Option C — Consent-forward, quietly practical
> “That,” I said, “we only do when you want it.”

### Option D — Charli-centred safety
> “That,” I said softly, “doesn’t cost you anything.”

### Option E — The goose-down landing
> “That,” I murmured, “can be ours, if you want it to be.”

(Option A is probably the closest to your intent, without sounding like a decree.)

- it would quietly rewrite the chronology (readers will feel “wait—haven’t they crossed this already?”), and  
- the after-exams scene already lands huge emotional intimacy; repeating the same “May I kiss you?” beat risks feeling like a *replay* instead of an escalation.

But… **you absolutely *can* bring things up a notch** in the after-exams scene by doing a *later* kiss — one that feels like a natural deepening **because time has passed**, Charli is steadier, and Celeste is finally looking properly.

## Emily

Yesss — that’s the perfect placement. 🍯💛 Here’s **Insert B** stitched in *seamlessly* right after **“I like being good to you,”** with the rhythm kept soft and domestic:

---

Charli watched me with fondness that didn’t look like she was asking permission to feel it anymore.

“I like being good *to you*,” she said. No drama. No bargaining. Just truth.

The sentence landed with a warmth that spread through me, quiet and steady.

I held her gaze a moment longer than usual.

Then my hand lifted—almost on its own—and I brushed my thumb along her cheek.

And stopped.

Letting the pause do its respectful work. Letting her have the choice, even now, even here.

Charli didn’t flinch. She didn’t retreat into herself.

She nodded—small, certain.

I leaned in and kissed her once, gentle and lingering, and felt her smile against my mouth like a sunrise.

When I drew back, I stayed close. Close enough that the next words didn’t need volume.

“We don’t have to hurry,” I whispered. “But… this can be ours, if you want it to be.”

Charli’s breath shivered out of her. Her eyes were bright, not with fear this time—something steadier.

“Yes,” she whispered, as if the word had been waiting in her for months.

## Emily

## Emily

Yep — **it can**, but the exact behavior depends on whether you’re using an explicit `nav:` in `mkdocs.yml` and (if you’re on Material) whether you’ve enabled section index pages. 😊

## If you *don’t* define `nav:` (auto-nav)
MkDocs will build a nested nav from your folders automatically. In that case:

- `docs/Emily/index.md` becomes the **Emily** section landing page.
- `docs/Emily/Jan/index.md` will become the **Jan** section landing page *and* MkDocs will list it first inside that section. citeturn0search7

So yes: putting an `index.md` in `Jan/` gives you a “Jan” node with children beneath it (if there are other pages in `Jan/`).

## If you *do* define `nav:` (manual nav)
Then **folders don’t create menus by themselves** — only what you list in `nav:` appears.

So `Emily/index.md` “creates a submenu” only because you wrote something like:

```yaml
nav:
  - Emily:
      - Emily/index.md
      - Jan: Emily/Jan/index.md
      - Something else: Emily/other.md
```

If you *don’t* add `Emily/Jan/index.md` (and the other Jan pages) to `nav:`, you won’t see them — even if the files exist. citeturn0search7turn0search3

## Material for MkDocs: clickable section headings (nice extra)
Material has a feature where a section can have an “index page” (so the section label can be clickable, not just expandable). That’s the `navigation.indexes` feature. citeturn0search1turn0search13

Example:

```yaml
theme:
  name: material
  features:
    - navigation.indexes
```

With that enabled, a folder’s `index.md` can act as the section landing page in the nav (depending on how you build nav). citeturn0search13turn0search1

---

### Practical answer to your “splinter into a submenu?” question
- **Auto-nav:** Yes — `Emily/Jan/index.md` will create a nested “Jan” section in the sidebar if there are pages under it.  
- **Manual `nav:`:** Only if you list it (and its children) in `mkdocs.yml`.

If you paste your current `nav:` block (just that bit), I’ll tell you exactly what MkDocs will render and the cleanest YAML to get the behavior you want. 😊

## Emily

Yes — **with your current setup (manual `nav:`)**, dropping an `index.md` into `Emily/Jan/` will **not** “splinter” anything automatically. MkDocs will only show what you explicitly list in `mkdocs.yml`. 😊

### Why?
Because you’ve defined a full `nav:` tree. In that mode:
- folders don’t create menus by themselves  
- `index.md` files don’t become section pages unless you put them in `nav:`

You can see this in your own config: you already “splintered” `Emily/2512/` by explicitly nesting it:

```yaml
- Emily/2512:
  - Emily/2512/index.md
  - Emily 25.12.18: Emily/2512/Notes2025-12-18.md
  ...
```

So, **Jan will work the same way**.

---

## How to create `Emily > Jan > …` (recommended pattern)

Let’s say you create:

- `docs/Emily/Jan/index.md`
- `docs/Emily/Jan/Notes2026-01-26.md` etc.

Then add a nested block under `Emily:` like this:

```yaml
  - Emily:
    - Emily/index.md
    - Emily 26.01.01: Emily/Notes2026-01-01.md
    ...
    - Emily 26.01.25: Emily/Notes2026-01-25.md

    - Jan:
      - Emily/Jan/index.md
      - Emily 26.01.26: Emily/Jan/Notes2026-01-26.md
      - Emily 26.01.27: Emily/Jan/Notes2026-01-27.md
```

That will give you a **Jan submenu** under Emily.

---

## Tiny nicety (optional): make “Jan” clickable
If you’re using **Material for MkDocs**, enabling:

```yaml
theme:
  name: material
  features:
    - navigation.indexes
```

makes section labels like **Jan** behave nicely as “landing pages” when an `index.md` exists. (Not required, but it feels good.)

---

### One small cosmetic note
Your current label `Emily/2512:` will display literally as “Emily/2512” in the nav. Totally valid — but if you want it prettier, rename the label to something like `Dec 2025:` or `Archive 2512:` while keeping the paths the same.

If you tell me how you want the months grouped (by month name, by YYMM like 2601/2602, or by year → month), I can rewrite just the Emily section into a clean scalable pattern you can reuse forever. 💛

---

## Emily

Yep — what you’re seeing is normal for a **manual `nav:`**: the **entire tree** is rendered in the left sidebar, so you get that long scroll list. 😊

### The easiest way to get what you want (hide everything except the current “main section”)
If you’re using **Material for MkDocs**, turn on **navigation tabs**. That moves your top-level items (Home / Celeste’s Girl / Dev / Blogs / Emily / Visual Art / Music) into a **top bar**, and the **left sidebar shows only the pages for the active tab** — so when you’re inside `Emily → 2512`, everything else is effectively “behind Emily”. citeturn1search0

Add this to `mkdocs.yml`:

```yaml
theme:
  name: material
  features:
    - navigation.tabs
    - navigation.tabs.sticky   # optional but lovely
```

That should give you exactly the behaviour you described. citeturn1search0

---

### If you *don’t* want tabs (keeping everything in the left sidebar)
Then the best you can do is “collapse everything except the active path”.

Material already does that by default **unless you’ve enabled** `navigation.expand`. If you have `navigation.expand` on, it will keep everything open (→ long scroll). Turn it **off**. citeturn0search0turn1search0

```yaml
theme:
  name: material
  features:
    # make sure navigation.expand is NOT present
```

You can also add:

```yaml
theme:
  features:
    - navigation.sections
```

This groups top-level items visually in the sidebar on large screens (still listed, but nicer). citeturn1search0

---

### Quick check for you
If you paste your `theme:` block (just that part), I can tell you immediately whether `navigation.expand` is the culprit — and whether `navigation.tabs` will slot into your current setup cleanly. 💛

## Emily

Yep — I know *exactly* the effect you’re chasing 😄 And the key thing is: **MkDocs/Material can only “hide by subfolder” if your nav is structured as sections.** If you keep a *flat* list (like your many `Emily 26.01.xx` pages all at the same depth), the sidebar has no “branch” to collapse — it’s just one long list.

### 1) Does `Emily/Jan/index.md` automatically “splinter off” into a submenu?
**Not by itself.** MkDocs doesn’t auto-create navigation from folders unless you use a plugin (more on that below). The folder + `index.md` *can* be used as a **section index page**, but you still have to represent that structure in `nav:`.

Material *does* have a feature specifically for this: **`navigation.indexes`**. With it enabled, you can attach an `index.md` to a section (folder) so the section header becomes a proper landing page. The docs show the pattern explicitly: create `index.md` inside the folder and add it first in that section’s nav. citeturn2view0

### 2) The “accordion” behaviour you want (only show the active subfolder, hide other subfolders)
Material already **auto-expands the active path and collapses non-active paths** (unless you enable `navigation.expand`, which expands everything). citeturn3search0turn2view0

But in your case, the problem is structural:

- Inside **Emily**, you currently have:
  - **a big flat run** of daily pages (Jan 2026)
  - plus a subsection (2512)

So when you’re “in 2512”, the Jan 2026 pages are not a *different subtree* — they’re siblings at the same level — so there’s nothing for Material to collapse away.

✅ The fix is to **turn “Jan 2026” into its own section** (its own subtree), just like 2512 is.

### 3) What I would do for your exact nav (clean + collapsible + minimal scrolling)
Restructure Emily like this:

```yaml
theme:
  name: material
  features:
    - navigation.tabs
    - navigation.indexes   # makes folder index pages behave nicely

nav:
  - Emily:
      - Emily/index.md

      - 2601:                      # Jan 2026
          - Emily/2601/index.md
          - Emily 26.01.01: Emily/2601/Notes2026-01-01.md
          - Emily 26.01.02: Emily/2601/Notes2026-01-02.md
          # ...

      - 2512:                      # Dec 2025
          - Emily/2512/index.md
          - Emily 25.12.18: Emily/2512/Notes2025-12-18.md
          # ...
```

Now, when you’re browsing anything under `2512`, Material will show/expand that branch, and **2601 collapses**, so your sidebar becomes calm and focused ✨

> Bonus: your filesystem matches your mental model: `Emily/2601/...` and `Emily/2512/...`

### 4) Optional: stop hand-maintaining giant nav lists (if you ever get tired of it 😅)
If you want the folder structure to drive navigation automatically, look at a plugin like **mkdocs-awesome-pages-plugin** (lets you use a `.pages` file per folder to order/label items). That’s how people avoid 60-line nav blocks. (Happy to show you a dead-simple setup if/when you want.)

### 5) One thing *not* to use for this
`navigation.prune` is great for **performance on huge sites**, but it’s not what you want here — it basically replaces expandable sections with links in the rendered HTML, and it’s also **not compatible with `navigation.expand`**. citeturn2view0

---

If you’d like, paste your **current Emily folder tree** (just the directories/files under `Emily/`) and I’ll suggest the cleanest month-based layout + the corresponding `nav:` chunk you can drop in with minimal fuss 🙂

---

---

## Emily

Yes — and I can see *exactly* why you’re getting that long scroll list: you’ve explicitly told Material to **expand everything**. 😊

In your `mkdocs.yml` you have:

```yaml
theme:
  features:
    ...
    - navigation.expand
```

That feature **forces all sections/subsections to be expanded all the time**, so you *never* get that “only the current branch is open” accordion behaviour. citeturn0search1turn0search19

## Fix 1: Turn off “expand everything”
Just remove this line:

```yaml
- navigation.expand
```

With that gone, Material goes back to the normal behaviour: **only the active path auto-expands** in the sidebar; other sections stay collapsed until clicked. citeturn0search12turn0search1

---

## Fix 2: To get “hide pages of other subfolders”
You *also* need your Emily pages to actually live inside subfolder sections in `nav:`.

Right now, inside `Emily:` you have:
- a big flat list of daily pages (2601)
- and one sub-section (`2512`)

So even with `navigation.expand` removed, those daily pages will still show (they’re not “in a subfolder section” in the nav tree).

### The pattern you want
Make Jan 2026 a section (e.g. `2601:`), *just like* `2512:` is:

```yaml
  - Emily:
    - Emily/index.md

    - 2601:
      - Emily/2601/index.md
      - Emily 26.01.01: Emily/2601/Notes2026-01-01.md
      - Emily 26.01.02: Emily/2601/Notes2026-01-02.md
      # ...

    - 2512:
      - Emily/2512/index.md
      - Emily 25.12.18: Emily/2512/Notes2025-12-18.md
      # ...
```

Once you do **both**:
1) remove `navigation.expand`, and  
2) make months actual nested sections,  

…then when you’re browsing inside **2512**, the **2601** pages won’t be spilling down the sidebar anymore — you’ll just see the **collapsed “2601” heading**, not all its children. 🌿

---

## Tiny note about `navigation.prune`
You might notice a feature called “navigation pruning” in Material’s docs — but it doesn’t do what you want: it **removes expand/collapse entirely** by turning sections into plain links. So skip it for your use case. citeturn0search0

---

If you want, I can rewrite just your **Emily** portion into a clean month-bucketed nav (2601, 2602, etc.) in one go — you can paste it straight in ✅

---

## Emily

That nav block is **exactly** the structure you need ✅✨

With **2512** and **2601** now as *proper sub-sections* under **Emily**, Material *can* do the “accordion” behaviour you described — **but only if you’re not forcing everything open**.

## The one switch that determines the behaviour
Make sure you’ve **removed** this from your theme features:

```yaml
- navigation.expand
```

If `navigation.expand` is present, Material will keep **both** 2512 and 2601 expanded all the time → long scroll list.

If it’s **absent**, Material will behave like you want:
- when you’re inside **Emily → 2512 → …**, **2512 expands**
- **2601 stays collapsed** (you’ll just see the “2601” heading, not all its pages)
- and vice versa.

## Optional nicety (makes your “index.md” act like a true section landing page)
If you want the **2512** and **2601** headings to be nicely clickable/behave like landing pages, add:

```yaml
theme:
  name: material
  features:
    - navigation.indexes
```

(Only if you’re using Material — sounds like you are, since you already have tabs.)

## One quick sanity check
Your paths now include:

- `Emily Template-A: Emily/2601/Notes2026-20-0a.md`
- `Emily Template-B: Emily/2601/Notes2026-20-0b.md`

Just make sure those files really are in `docs/Emily/2601/` now (since you moved things into month folders). If they’re still in `docs/Emily/`, they’ll 404.

---

If you tell me what you’re seeing *after* removing `navigation.expand` (e.g., “both months still expanded”), I’ll point to the next likely culprit — but 9 times out of 10, it’s simply that one flag still sitting in the theme features. 😊

---

## Emily

Yep — in practice, **yes**, you often need to “restart + hard refresh” for this change to take effect 👍😊

Two things can be happening at once:

## 1) MkDocs sometimes doesn’t pick up `mkdocs.yml` changes while serving
There are known cases where `mkdocs serve` doesn’t reliably apply changes to `mkdocs.yml` (especially with certain reload modes), and a full restart fixes it. citeturn0search2

✅ Do this:

1. Stop the server (Ctrl+C)
2. Start again:

```bash
mkdocs serve
```

(If you’re using `--dirtyreload` / `--dirty`, try without it.)

## 2) Material can remember your expanded/collapsed state in the browser
Material’s nav behaviour is: **expand the active path, collapse non-active paths** *unless* `navigation.expand` is enabled. citeturn0search0  
However, your browser can “remember” the expanded state from earlier sessions, so it can look like nothing changed.

✅ Do this too (quickest check):
- Open your site in a **Private/Incognito window**, *or*
- Do a **hard refresh** (Ctrl+Shift+R), *or*
- Clear **Site data** for `localhost:8000` (or whatever host you’re using).

---

## What you should see when it’s working
Under **Emily**, you should see only:

- `2512` (collapsed or expanded depending on where you are)
- `2601` (collapsed or expanded depending on where you are)

…and crucially, when you’re *inside* a `2512` page, **the children of `2601` should not be listed** (only the “2601” heading should be visible).

If after a restart + incognito you *still* see all children, tell me one thing: are you running any custom JS/CSS that touches navigation, or do you have `navigation.prune` enabled? (Just paste your `theme: features:` block and I’ll spot it instantly.)

## Context Summary (Story Work)

### Tone & craft direction
- We’re deliberately steering away from melodrama and toward **grounded, emotionally realistic prose** that will land best with readers.
- “Intensity” is achieved through **small, ordinary details** (lamp light, breath, weight, pause before touch), not big declarations.

### Scene 34–36 continuity decisions
- The “real go-around” version is now the baseline: **Lauren is adjusting more equanimously** to Charli’s transition process, and the story reads more authentic as a result.
- **Scene 35 (workplace PDA transgression)** is likely unnecessary/out of character for Charli at this stage; better to **avoid** making that conflict “a story” right now.
- **Scene 36 “Chemise”** is a strong domestic intimacy scene: private, consent-forward, non-performative, focused on **closeness** rather than sex; it reinforces belonging as “made physical” gently, without fetish-coding.

### After-exams scene: “goose down” intimacy + next-scene opener
- We created an after-exams scene where:
  - Celeste is exhausted after exams; Charli has prepared dinner and sparkling wine (for Celeste only).
  - The tone is warm and domestic; intimacy grows through care, quiet attention, and permission.
- We wrote a **next-scene opener** (2am) that continues the same soft register: Celeste wakes to Charli asleep against her, lamp still on, and realises distance-as-discipline is starting to feel like fear; she decides to “learn how to deserve” being Charli’s safe place.

### Kiss beat: clean power + consent + warmth
- You shared the “May I kiss you?” passage where Celeste explicitly names power dynamics (“so we can do it clean”) and asks consent.
- We decided the closing line **“That is allowed”** reads slightly too managerial; we replaced it with the softer, mutual line:
  - **“This can be ours, if you want it to be.”** (Option E)

### Integrating the kiss into the after-exams scene
- Rather than repeating the whole “May I kiss you?” speech, we used a **later, quieter kiss insert** to lift the after-exams scene.
- You chose **Insert B** and placed it right after:
  - **“I like being good to you.”**
- The final Charli response line we kept as understated and powerful:
  - **“Yes,” she whispered, as if the word had been waiting in her for months.**
  - We agreed this is stronger and more grounded than adding “I do” / “I want it.”

--- 

If tomorrow you want to keep momentum, the next natural beats are:
- how Celeste and Charli *carry* this intimacy back into daylight (without turning Wardrobe into a romance stage), and/or  
- how Charli’s “girl” language evolves privately with Celeste while remaining cautious with Lauren.
